<div id="review_1203325967" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1203325967" />
    <a title="Penny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7463065-penny"><img alt="Penny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1420145167p2/7463065.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1203325967?book_show_action=true">Feb 17, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Penny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Penny" href="/user/show/7463065-penny">Penny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7463065-penny?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7463065-penny?shelf=y-read-young-adults">y-read-young-adults</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7463065-penny?shelf=likereviews">likereviews</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1203325967" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11109656395997055286">I liked it but I have a few problems with it.<br/><br/>This is a young-adult book, yet, I struggled a lot trying to remember the ages of the characters, I kept aging them in my mind. I had no problems with Rachel, she is a teenager and a pushover through and through, but the rest…not so much. Isaiah seems older than he is supposed to be, and the people around him do too. Like Eric for example, seriously, a 19 year old that controls the street racing bets… I don't know, I had problems believing it, so in m</span>
  <span id="freeText11109656395997055286" style="display:none">I liked it but I have a few problems with it.<br /><br />This is a young-adult book, yet, I struggled a lot trying to remember the ages of the characters, I kept aging them in my mind. I had no problems with Rachel, she is a teenager and a pushover through and through, but the rest…not so much. Isaiah seems older than he is supposed to be, and the people around him do too. Like Eric for example, seriously, a 19 year old that controls the street racing bets… I don't know, I had problems believing it, so in my mind most of the characters were older. <br /><br />Then, for me the story was unbalanced. On one side, we have a street topic like car racing, bets, rapes, beatings, drugs, etc. These kinds of things seem more mature in general, not that suited or relatable to teenagers, yet Rachel confronts this fine, ok, no problem, it seems to me that she should have struggled at least a little bit with it. But then, on the other hand, we have an age appropriate topic like sex is for a 17 year old, and this however, is conducted more as if Rachel was a 15 year old. It was way too light, more so in comparison with the hardness of the other aspects of the story. The contrast between the two sides made the book lack credibility for me.<br /> <br />Also, it would have been nice to see Rachel <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[confront her family about Isaiah and try to fight for him and make them see reason.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>Instead, in the end happened what happened (I'm not going to say), and that conflict was avoided. I don't think that is how it would happen in most instances of real life so it was a bit disappointing to see the “easy” exit that the writer took to avoid all that.<br /><br />Generally speaking, all and all, it was a nice story.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11109656395997055286" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_732116458" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/732116458" />
    <a title="Giselle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5789353-giselle"><img alt="Giselle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605042512p2/5789353.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/732116458?book_show_action=true">Oct 01, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Giselle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Giselle" href="/user/show/5789353-giselle">Giselle</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5789353-giselle?shelf=4-star">4-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5789353-giselle?shelf=requested-for-review">requested-for-review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5789353-giselle?shelf=2013">2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5789353-giselle?shelf=genre-romance">genre-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5789353-giselle?shelf=from-netgalley">from-netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5789353-giselle?shelf=genre-contemporary">genre-contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5789353-giselle?shelf=age-new-adult">age-new-adult</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer732116458" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15203086585727880520">Rachel is labeled as "odd and strange" by her peers. She's quiet and typically a loner. It also doesn't help that she's not your girlie-girl, she'd rather dive under the hood of a car and change the oil instead of shopping at the mall like a "normal" teenage girl. Then she meets bad boy Isaiah who brings out the best in her. When they both end up in trouble with a criminal on the streets, they have to work together and end up teaching each other that love is the most powerful force that drives t</span>
  <span id="freeText15203086585727880520" style="display:none">Rachel is labeled as "odd and strange" by her peers. She's quiet and typically a loner. It also doesn't help that she's not your girlie-girl, she'd rather dive under the hood of a car and change the oil instead of shopping at the mall like a "normal" teenage girl. Then she meets bad boy Isaiah who brings out the best in her. When they both end up in trouble with a criminal on the streets, they have to work together and end up teaching each other that love is the most powerful force that drives them.<br /><br />Told in alternate point of views from both Rachel and Isaiah, we get to see how strongly vivid and different their personalities and livelihood really is. It's the cliche rich girl meets bad boy story, but it has a lot of heart and emotion. Though the way they fall in love so quickly, I don't really dismiss it because at that age it can happen. I didn't even think it was super cheesy because the two characters thought out the best in one another and that's what real love does. I wasn't a big fan of the overly dramatic torture that both characters went through..it was almost like they weren't ever going to get their happy ending and you know they needed it desperately. I love how there was a big part of the dysfunctional family dynamics at play. No one is perfect, no one is exempt to circumstance and it's fairly evident Katie McGarry was showing this. I also loved how her brothers are like overprotective bears. They really just love her and want to shield her from pain. Not to mention that they're all pretty swoon-worthy themselves LOL<br /><br />Overall, if you're looking for a contemporary, emotional, sizzling, dramatic YA read, pick one of McGarry's books. You'll gobble them up like candy!<br /><br /><br />RATING 4/5<br /><br />QUOTES<br /><br />“God does exist and he sent angel in a white Mustang to prove it.” (38)<br /><br />“Why on earth would a guy like him want to be anywhere near a girl like me?” (59)<br /><br />“I like how Isaiah looks at me as if I'm the only girl in the world. Or like an antelope he's going to pounce on.” (88)<br /><br />“What people project to the world never shows what's lurking on the inside.” (125)<br /><br />“Worrying is all I'm good at.” (193)<br /><br />“You can ignore me, Rachel, and you can try to treat me as a friend, but none of that will erase the fact that I think about kissing you every second I'm awake and dream at night of my hands on your body. And it sure as hell won't erase that I'm terrified by how much I like you.” (223)<br /><br />“I feel like a mouse with you. The one that's already been caught by the cat.” (236)<br /><br />“My entire life is one thick rope full of knots and links where people have twisted me inside and out.” (284)<br /><br />“I don't know what love is or how it should feel, but I know that when I'm with you I like who I am, and that's never happened to me before.” (285)<br /><br />“Life isn't made-for-television movies or books with happy-ever-afters. Sometimes the choices we're presented with are bad or worse.” (309)<br /><br />“I'm blessed. I have so much more than others, and on the outside my family is absolutely perfect.” (343)</span>

<div id="review_505094683" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/505094683" />
    <a title="Glass" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4808910-glass"><img alt="Glass" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1583244629p2/4808910.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/505094683?book_show_action=true">Jan 13, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Glass" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Glass" href="/user/show/4808910-glass">Glass</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/17679547-crash-into-you">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4808910-glass?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4808910-glass?shelf=girls-reading-together">girls-reading-together</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4808910-glass?shelf=harlequin">harlequin</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4808910-glass?shelf=tanja-zemira-miss-glass-book-club">tanja-zemira-miss-glass-book-club</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer505094683" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer509737877709073656">Review from <a href='http://jacitamati.blogspot.com/2013/11/arc-review-crash-into-you-by-katie.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Ja čitam, a ti?</a><br/><b>Tanja:</b> I have no idea where to start this one, girl. I mean we have been waiting for Isaiah's story for so long. Boy, finally.<br/><br/><b>Glass:</b> I've been waiting for Isaiah's story... forever. My heart broke for that sweet, tattooed bad boy in the first book, Pushing the Limits.<br/><br/><b>Tanja:</b> Yes, also I'm so happy that we finally see him more than just a tattooed bad boy. He is so more than that. Remember when in Dare You To, Beth broke his heart? I cried so much for him and here I cont</span>
  <span id="freeText509737877709073656" style="display:none">Review from <a href="http://jacitamati.blogspot.com/2013/11/arc-review-crash-into-you-by-katie.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Ja čitam, a ti?</a><br /><b>Tanja:</b> I have no idea where to start this one, girl. I mean we have been waiting for Isaiah's story for so long. Boy, finally.<br /><br /><b>Glass:</b> I've been waiting for Isaiah's story... forever. My heart broke for that sweet, tattooed bad boy in the first book, Pushing the Limits.<br /><br /><b>Tanja:</b> Yes, also I'm so happy that we finally see him more than just a tattooed bad boy. He is so more than that. Remember when in Dare You To, Beth broke his heart? I cried so much for him and here I continued to do so. Basically my heart ached for him throughout all three books. Even though deep down you know he'll find his safe heaven, Katie throw some unexpected twists here. But let's introduce Rachel first. What do you think girl? I always wanted to have a huge family and few older brothers, but now I'm not so sure.<br /><br /><b>Glass:</b> Me too, but I think it was more that we were delusional that they would be our big, strong protectors and we'd be little princesses. Well, we know better now. To be completely honest with you, I wasn't the biggest fan of Rachel when I first started reading Crash into You - she looked too dramatic for me and not very convincing with whole fragile good girl/cars lover image. I'm still not one hundred percent sold on that idea, but I got to understand her. But, speaking about Beth, I kind of hated her in this book...<br /><br /><b>Tanja:</b> I wasn't convinced at the start either. But yeah I could understand her, that's for sure. We all want to make our parents happy, I guess. Ah, yes! I wanted to slap her when she started acting like nothing happened. What do you say about Abby, Isaiah's friend? I really liked her and I'd love to see her book too.<br /><br /><b>Glass:</b> Oh, she is my favorite female character in this book - you know how much I love kick-ass girls. I really hope that Katie McGarry will give us her story too, but I think hers would be the darkest book in the series so far. It looks like she had tough life and that she was forced to do a lot of things she didn't want to.<br />But let me tell you - Crash into You has the best first kiss scene ever!<br /><br /><b>Tanja:</b> Oh, hell yes!! It was the hottest and the most innocent first kiss in the world of YA first kisses I've read so far. Even I got goosebumps. I don't think that any kiss after that one was so strong and emotional. But then again we're used to Katie writing emotional and powerful scenes. Did you have any troubles with this book. I've got a few. First one is Rachel's parents. I wanted to slap them both. (and I do respect older people)<br /><br /><b>Glass:</b> Me too. At first I was most annoyed with her mother, but later her father. Even older brothers had few not very likable moments. My biggest problem with this book is the fact that it reminded me too much of Perfect Chemistry series and lot less of previous books Katie McGarry's novels. All that street/ghetto background of the story wasn't quite believable - it felt little bit "fake". It's not that I didn't loved this book, I just had impression as if I was reading modern fairy tale about princess and stable boy.<br /><br /><b>Tanja:</b> True that. I loved every emotional aspect of this story but like you said, setting was sometimes off. That's basically the main reason why for me, this book is the weakest in this series. It's still a five star read but Dare You To was more coherent to me. So West's story is next. What are your expectations?<br /><br /><b>Glass:</b> Honestly, not much. I'm not completely sure how long this series will be interesting to the readers. She already gave us stories of three central characters - everything else is just playing on safe card. I think it is time for her to write something completely different, don't you think? But Tanja, we will read sequel! No matter everything I said. Got it?<br /><br /><b>Tanja:</b> I totally agree, Somehow I think Katie should move on and give us something new (but after we get Abby's story). You're the boss, girl. Till then we're gonna reread that first kiss scene. *wink*<br /><br /><i>***Copy of this book provided by publisher via NetGalley in exchange for an honest review.***</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="509737877709073656" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_759191803" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/759191803" />
    <a title="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library"><img alt="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1350750103p2/4551536.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/759191803?book_show_action=true">Nov 07, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" href="/user/show/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library">Maja (The Nocturnal Library)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781848452541" href="/book/show/18454323-crash-into-you">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=arc-2013">arc-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=alternating-povs">alternating-povs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=contemporary-fiction">contemporary-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=failed-to-impress">failed-to-impress</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=incredibly-stupid-choices">incredibly-stupid-choices</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=reviewed-in-2013">reviewed-in-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=horrible-whiner">horrible-whiner</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=mira-ink">mira-ink</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer759191803" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9620827300596854078"><b>2.5 stars</b><br/>The definition of insanity is doing the same thing over and over again and expecting different results. Well then, methinks I’m batshit crazy because I just never learn. <br/><br/>Even though I’m fully aware that she has many, many fans, Katie McGarry’s books never quite worked for me. I often found her approach to certain subjects too shallow, her characters just a tiny bit plastic and her writing awfully clichéd. They are, for me, the type of books I can finish in one sitting, and then promptly</span>
  <span id="freeText9620827300596854078" style="display:none"><b>2.5 stars</b><br>The definition of insanity is doing the same thing over and over again and expecting different results. Well then, methinks I’m batshit crazy because I just never learn. <br><br>Even though I’m fully aware that she has many, many fans, Katie McGarry’s books never quite worked for me. I often found her approach to certain subjects too shallow, her characters just a tiny bit plastic and her writing awfully clichéd. They are, for me, the type of books I can finish in one sitting, and then promptly forget they exist.<br><br>The same stands true for Crash Into You, albeit somewhat amplified. Despite my lukewarm feelings towards the previous two books, I found myself looking forward to Isaiah’s story. Of all McGarry’s characters, he’s the one I felt had the most potential. But instead of building upon the promising foundations, McGarry turned him into one of those bad-on-the-outside-decent-on-the-inside archetypal romance heroes, thus effectively ruining his character and the overall story for me. Where was the expected depth? Mommy issues and a few false rumors do not a hero make.<br><br>Back when Isaiah thought himself in love with Beth, I wholeheartedly agreed that they weren’t right for each other. Two severely damaged individuals would always drag each other down, no matter their intentions. But who he got instead wasn’t much better for him, and she was a disappointment for me as a reader as well. I was promised a street racer, and instead I got a skittish, never-been-kissed girl with no backbone and more issues than I could count. So even though Isaiah ended up being as stereotypical as they come, the real letdown was Rachel.<br><br>With her personality and her will practically smothered by her family, Rachel grew up into a weak, strange girl prone to panic attacks. Her small rebellion, the street race where she met Isaiah, was a once-in-a-lifetime deal, not a common occurrence like the book description led me to believe. There were so many times I wanted to shake some sense into Rachel, make her stand up to her family instead of cowering and throwing up until her throat was raw and bleeding. Their relationship was at times exaggerated to the point of being ridiculous, which is exactly what McGarry usually does and why her books rarely work for me. <br><br>As always, secondary characters were far more interesting, probably because they haven’t been turned into clichés just yet. Abby has a great story to tell, McGarry has hinted at a horrible past that I would normally be excited to explore. My problem is that I don’t trust this author to do it properly, without turning Abby into a textbook teen martyr, a troubled girl only waiting for the right boy to solve all her problems. The next book isn’t Abby’s, however, that dubious honor belongs to Rachel’s brother West.<br><br>I’ve decided to part ways with McGarry so many times, only to pick up the newest title as soon as it becomes available. This time, I know better than to make such statements. I don’t feel particularly drawn to West’s story, but once it comes out… who knows? <br><br><a href="http://www.thenocturnallibrary.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380226536i/681142.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="9620827300596854078" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_503651005" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/503651005" />
    <a title="AJ" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3143126-aj"><img alt="AJ" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1406382884p2/3143126.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/503651005?book_show_action=true">Jan 11, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="AJ" class="user" itemprop="url" name="AJ" href="/user/show/3143126-aj">AJ</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3143126-aj?shelf=drama">drama</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3143126-aj?shelf=series-standalone">series-standalone</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3143126-aj?shelf=romantic">romantic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3143126-aj?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer503651005" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13554831465673364470">After <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10194514.Pushing_the_Limits__Pushing_the_Limits___1_' title='Pushing the Limits (Pushing the Limits, #1) by Katie McGarry' rel='nofollow noopener'>Pushing the Limits</a> completely rocked my world last year, I promised myself that I would read everything that Katie McGarry publishes, and three books later, I’m not regretting my decision one little bit. <i>Crash Into You</i> finally brings the story of Isaiah – the tattooed, pierced, car-obsessed bad boy that I fell for when I first met him as Noah’s best friend in PTL. <br/><br/>At 17 years old he is a true victim of ‘the system’, he has been moved from foster home to foster home since he was 6 years old</span>
  <span id="freeText13554831465673364470" style="display:none">After <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10194514.Pushing_the_Limits__Pushing_the_Limits___1_" title="Pushing the Limits (Pushing the Limits, #1) by Katie McGarry" rel="nofollow noopener">Pushing the Limits</a> completely rocked my world last year, I promised myself that I would read everything that Katie McGarry publishes, and three books later, I’m not regretting my decision one little bit. <i>Crash Into You</i> finally brings the story of Isaiah – the tattooed, pierced, car-obsessed bad boy that I fell for when I first met him as Noah’s best friend in PTL. <br /><br />At 17 years old he is a true victim of ‘the system’, he has been moved from foster home to foster home since he was 6 years old, feeling completely unwanted and unloved, and has developed a tough persona to help him survive. After being left broken hearted by the girl he thought he loved, Isaiah is one angry boy, but on the inside, he considers himself broken. But OMG, you’ve gotta love him! Despite his badass exterior, he has a massive heart, is determined to make a good life for himself, and is unwaveringly loyal to those he considers his family. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“Noah and I — we’re brothers despite not sharing blood, and Echo became my sister the day she put a smile on his face. They’re my family and I’m going to fight to keep what’s mine.”</i>
</blockquote><br />But to have the life he wants, he needs money, and the only way to get it is to do what he does best – race cars. A bit of a legend on the street racing scene, he is all geared up to race one night when ridiculously naïve and innocent Rachel rocks up looking for a race of her own. <br /><br />Also 17 years old, Rachel leads a very sheltered life. She is rich and privileged, but has a severely effed up family life that has left her shy and frightened with significant anxiety issues. She lives her life to please others, but secretly cars are her passion, and she craves the excitement of racing in order to have something for herself. When she gets in way over her head, good guy Isaiah comes to her rescue, and the two of them find themselves in a situation where their very lives are in danger and they have to work together in order to save themselves. <br /><br />What follows is a beautifully unfolding love story of two teenagers from completely different backgrounds who are fighting not only to be together, but also to live their lives on their own terms.<br /><br />Oh Isaiah! How I love you! Instantly drawn to Rachel, he is beautifully protective of her, and incredibly respectful, recognizing that she is not from his world. She’s adorably innocent - good, pure, and trusting, and everything that Isaiah has never had, or thinks that he deserves. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“I’m still not good enough for a girl like her, but she’s back in my life and she needs someone to protect her. I’ll fill the role and absorb as much of her light as I can before she leaves me behind in the darkness.”</i>
</blockquote><br />I have found that when you have a romantic storyline where one person doesn’t feel worthy of the other, it’s a very fine line between heartache and absolute irritation, but Katie McGarry does it brilliantly. Isaiah’s battle to recover from his heartbreak, realize and accept his feelings for Rachel and then find the strength and the confidence to act on them is absolutely beautiful. He is understandably wary, but isn’t afraid to let his feelings be known, and the way he opens up to Rachel and gives her his heart is absolutely beautiful. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“I don’t want to be without you. I like who I am with you, and I don’t want to go back to who I was before.” <br />“I love you, Rachel. So this will work. No matter what or who stands in our way.”<br /><br /><b>“I can’t give you the world, Rachel, but I’ll give you all I got.”</b></i>
</blockquote><br />Rachel is an interesting heroine. Her home life is awful, and she has all sorts of issues stemming from that. But she finds that she is different around Isaiah, feeling a connection with him that puts her at ease and gives her the confidence to be the kind of person she’s always wanted to be, and I loved seeing her come out of her shell. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“This isn’t me. None of it. I’m not the girl who hangs in a bar. I’m not the girl who is comfortable talking to guys. And I’m sure not the girl who leans over the table to be close to anyone. <br />Yet I’m doing all those things and I’m loving every freaking second.”</i>
</blockquote><br />She does have major confidence issues, and that leads to a few moments of regression that made me want to smack her, but I love that once they start to open up to each other, Isaiah is the kind of guy who is going to let her be stupid, and he manages to set her straight. <br /><br />And while the overprotectiveness of her four older brothers is stifling (including the hero of the next book in the series, West – another bad boy), it’s clear that they love and care for her deeply, and I really liked her moments with them. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“You don’t kiss boys,” says West. “Boys shouldn’t be anywhere near you. Guys only want one thing, Rach, and it ain’t conversation. I should know.” He waves off the subject in frustration, then shakes his head as he speaks again. “Why are we even talking about this? You aren’t seeing anyone.” <br />“Ah, hell,” mumbles Jack. “We’re having the sex talk with my baby sister.” <br />“Is she dating?” Gavin demands of West and Ethan. “She can’t be dating. Now we have to beat the snot out of some horny teenager. You should have told me this was going on.” <br />“Make them stop,” I whisper to Ethan. Along with the dread of speeches and vomiting, I’m also dying of embarrassment. <br />“She’s not dating!” West shudders as if spiders cover him. “That’s just sick, Rach. Don’t talk like that. Ever. Again.”</i>
</blockquote><br />With chapters in alternating POVs, Isaiah and Rachel’s individual stories are really well developed and a little bit heartbreaking. I loved the inclusion of Noah, Echo, Beth, Logan, and even Mrs Collins in the story, and new character Abby is definitely one I hope we’ll see again.<br /><br />But as usual it’s all about the romance, and this is absolutely gorgeous. Rachel is new to boys, and so she just blindly throws herself out there, which is really refreshing. And Isaiah is so incredibly sweet with her - the little grins whenever he sees her, the linking of their fingers, the sweet way he brushes his fingers over her cheeks and steamy kisses in the backseat of the car. It’s a YA swoon-fest, and I absolutely loved it! <br /><br />With all of this intertwined with the complex world of street racing, there’s a lot going on. And although I did find this book really long and a little bit slow going at times, there were definitely a few surprises in there and the overall story is a really beautiful one – and I loved getting to see Isaiah finally get his HEA. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“The way she curls in my arms makes me feel like I’m the hero. I like being her hero. I like the way her eyes shine at me, the way her body melts when I touch her, her soft lips on mine. I love her warmth and every curve. <br />I love her.”</i>
</blockquote><br />Oh swoon!<br /><br />Loved it – 4 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13554831465673364470" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14300889369551332901">Can I please give this book more than 5 stars?!<br/><br/>This is an absolutely take-your-breath-away, tears-streaming-down-your-face, AMAZING read!<br/><br/>I love Isaiah and Rachel so much it's insane.   <span id="freeText14300889369551332901" style="display:none">Can I please give this book more than 5 stars?!<br /><br />This is an absolutely take-your-breath-away, tears-streaming-down-your-face, AMAZING read!<br /><br />I love Isaiah and Rachel so much it's insane. I was captivated by their love and how it made them stronger and overcame all of the struggles in their lives. I completely believed that as long as they had each other, everything would work out. This book got super intense and serious and I just felt so pulled in to the story and couldn't help but keep turning the pages. This is the kind of book that you read and all of a sudden you realize you've read 100 pages and didn't even know it. There is never a slow point! <br />I feel like their love is real and they are real. I don't want this story to be over!!! <br />I love the whole car and racing elements, it made it super unique and interesting. Rachel is a very relatable character and I felt like I could relate to her on some levels, and I'm sure many other people can too. I love how Isaiah has a hard exterior, but in reality he has just had a hard life, and wants to be loved. I want to just give him a hug! Both of these characters had to learn what loving someone means, and how to let yourself be loved. Their journey is a beautiful one.<br />That ending almost killed me though, but I love how it turned out and it just made the story so real. It truly shows the depth of Rachel and Isaiah's love and how pure it is.<br /><br />Wonderful contemporary read!!</span>

  <span id="freeText6697776207320552081" style="display:none">4.5 Stars!<br><br>Another great addition to the series. <div id="review_536394067" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/536394067" />
    <a title="Melanie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10890208-melanie"><img alt="Melanie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1413275441p2/10890208.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/536394067?book_show_action=true">Feb 14, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melanie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melanie" href="/user/show/10890208-melanie">Melanie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781743564967" href="/book/show/18334685-crash-into-you">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=could-have-been-so-much-better">could-have-been-so-much-better</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=take-your-instant-love-and-get-lost">take-your-instant-love-and-get-lost</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=me-likes-you">me-likes-you</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10890208-melanie?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer536394067" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8402219478375237691">See more reviews at <a href='http://yamidnightreads.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>YA Midnight Reads</a><br/><br/><b>Thank you Harlequin Australia for sending me this copy. No comepensation was given or taken to alter this review. </b><br/><blockquote>
  <br/>
  <p>“I love you, Rachel. So this will work. No matter what or who stands in our way.”</p>
  <br/>
</blockquote><br/>I see a trend going on. Third book syndrome. Where books get underwhelming (Allegiant, Requiem etc). It's not to say that Crash Into You was a complete disaster, but definitely not what I had in mind from such a promising and fun series so far.<br/><br/>We start off w</span>
  <span id="freeText8402219478375237691" style="display:none">See more reviews at <a href="http://yamidnightreads.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">YA Midnight Reads</a><br /><br /><b>Thank you Harlequin Australia for sending me this copy. No comepensation was given or taken to alter this review. </b><br /><blockquote>
  <br />
  <p>“I love you, Rachel. So this will work. No matter what or who stands in our way.”</p>
  <br />
</blockquote><br />I see a trend going on. Third book syndrome. Where books get underwhelming (Allegiant, Requiem etc). It's not to say that Crash Into You was a complete disaster, but definitely not what I had in mind from such a promising and fun series so far.<br /><br />We start off with two total opposites. Rachel comes from a wealthy family, she gets what she wants. She's seen as a perfect child--but that's not who she really is. Her mother tries to make Rachel a replica of her deceased older sister, Colleen and her overbearing brothers are always protecting Rachel from other people at school, but it feels like it makes matters worse. She also gets panic attacks. Only she doesn't dare to tell her family. Her job is to make her mother happy. And she's getting sick of it. I genuinely believe that I would slip into Rachel's shoes smoothly, empathy her suffocating situation. Unfortunately, I could not. Her constant inner-wallowing about her convoluted family crept underneath my skin. In other words--crazily annoying. Per contra, I loved the intricate family that Katie McGarry constructed. It felt authentic despite the large amount of problems--believable or not--that channelled around.<br /><br />We all knew and fell in love with Isaiah in Pushing The Limits and Dare You To, so when we found out he was to have his own book, no one couldn't wait. And, when I finally got my hands on this novel, I wasn't disappointed. Isaiah's POV was my favourite. He has his struggles but is mentally strong to battle them. With him recently hurt by Beth's rejection of his love and now living with Noah (yes we get some Noah and Echo! Even Beth :D) and reunited with his mum again, he is only just keeping his head above water.<br /><br />My main issue with Crash Into You, apart from my repulsion towards Rachel, was the chemistry. Why? Instant. Love. Angst. No go. However, unlike other romances, Crash Into You still had a convincing relationship, but it fast fowarded too quickly. A build-up between the two would have been much better. Furthermore, I appreciated that there was a plot line going on. I have a huge COLOSSAL love for a plot line other than: he loves me, he loves me not. She loves me, she loves me not.<br /><br />Even though I was not head over heels about Rachel and the romance, Crash Into You was still a very much likable and entertaining novel. Katie McGarry is still on my auto-read list. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8402219478375237691" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_533145840" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/533145840" />
    <a title="Patrycja" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6852653-patrycja"><img alt="Patrycja" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1586460589p2/6852653.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/533145840?book_show_action=true">Feb 11, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Patrycja" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Patrycja" href="/user/show/6852653-patrycja">Patrycja</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6852653-patrycja?shelf=2013">2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6852653-patrycja?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer533145840" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17508522840602939593"><br/>I was anticipating Isaiah’s story, more than I did with Beth and Ryan’s. From the beginning I was very smitten with him – I was literally hooked on his ‘bad boy’ image, tortured past and broken heart. Isaiah’s passion for tattoos, cars and racing is definitely panty dropping, so I hoped Katie McGarry will show her true talent and picture amazing, swoon worthy male that will make my heart beat faster. <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1386844565i/7457304._SY540_.jpg' width='400' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Partly, she did so. Why only partly? I think I forgot Crash Into You is young adult novel which </span>
  <span id="freeText17508522840602939593" style="display:none"><br>I was anticipating Isaiah’s story, more than I did with Beth and Ryan’s. From the beginning I was very smitten with him – I was literally hooked on his ‘bad boy’ image, tortured past and broken heart. Isaiah’s passion for tattoos, cars and racing is definitely panty dropping, so I hoped Katie McGarry will show her true talent and picture amazing, swoon worthy male that will make my heart beat faster. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1386844565i/7457304._SY540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Partly, she did so. Why only partly? I think I forgot Crash Into You is young adult novel which made me miss steam factor and maturity in characters. I found myslef hoping for 18+ version ;)<br>Despite that, I really enjoyed Crash Into You. For seventeen year old, Isaiah was phenomenal character and I would love to read about twenty seven year old version of him. That would be something off the charts amazing! He totally would steal my heart then. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1386844565i/7457305._SX540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I wasn’t very happy with Rachel’s creation, though. I was hoping she’d be more badass and crazy chick. I thought kick ass girl would be wonderful match for Isaiah. Instead, Rachel is same old good, rich girl that is a fan of cars. Here, I honestly hoped for more. <br><br>Her family drama was well thought, but few times I wanted to scream and shake Rachel’s brothers and parents. I was shocked how incredibly blind and selfish a family could be.<br>What I did enjoy? <br><br>I definitely liked the car racing parts. I’m not a fan of mechanics in real life, but I absolutely had fun while reading about it. I think car racers are exceptionally sexy, and McGarry really well pictured them. I also did like Rachel and Isaiah together. Of course, I craved a little bit of sexy times, but still on young adult level they did get pretty hot and bothered without being completely intimate. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1386844565i/7457306.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Overall, Crash Into You is a book I would swoon and melt over two years ago, when I was in young adult phase. Now, I’m kind of one or two levels up, and I miss the maturity and intimate aspects that are pictured in adult romance novels. Yet, I did enjoy Isaiah and Rachel’s story. And I greatly believe that fans of ‘lighter’ romance books or people who are not comfortable with sexual encounters on the pages, will fall head over heels in love with Katie McGarry’s book. <br></span>
  <a data-text-id="17508522840602939593" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('FbqKhps0l50uKAy4BtItpsA64EpDGOMC9nscWkbrfX9J+7YntS7WgjbnUy5XcnRg/ixsA4NuHhTRQVkPWalw1Q==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('P+5asJRaNIlgEEC0gjHyo0c/+qihx7nPDVRCcXsZ5wFjr2YRukB1lnjfHyLTkatleSl24WGxRNkqbgckZFvqqw==')})
  }
